                if (solution.style.display != 'none') {
                    solution.style.display = 'none';

                    link.className = 'solution_link_show';

<script type="text/javascript">
//<![CDATA[



/* JQUERY */
jQuery(document).ready(function(){ 
    
   
  

	/* jQuery('ul#rmenu').superfish(); */
	/* jQuery('ul#rmenu').superfish().find('ul').bgIframe({opacity:false}); */
 
	/* For IE6 */
	if (jQuery.browser.msie && /MSIE 6\.0/i.test(window.navigator.userAgent) && !/MSIE 7\.0/i.test(window.navigator.userAgent) && !/MSIE 8\.0/i.test(window.navigator.userAgent)) {

		/* Max-width for images in IE6 */		
		var centerwidth = jQuery("td#middle").width(); 
		
		/* Images without caption */
		jQuery(".post img").each(function() { 
			var maxwidth = centerwidth - 10 + 'px';
			var imgwidth = jQuery(this).width(); 
			var imgheight = jQuery(this).height(); 
			var newimgheight = (centerwidth / imgwidth * imgheight) + 'px';	
			if (imgwidth > centerwidth) { 
				jQuery(this).css({width: maxwidth}); 
				jQuery(this).css({height: newimgheight}); 
			}
		});
		
		/* Images with caption */
		jQuery("div.wp-caption").each(function() { 
			var captionwidth = jQuery(this).width(); 
			var maxcaptionwidth = centerwidth + 'px';
			var captionheight = jQuery(this).height();
			var captionimgwidth =  jQuery("div.wp-caption img").width();
			var captionimgheight =  jQuery("div.wp-caption img").height();
			if (captionwidth > centerwidth) { 
				jQuery(this).css({width: maxcaptionwidth}); 
				var newcaptionheight = (centerwidth / captionwidth * captionheight) + 'px';
				var newcaptionimgheight = (centerwidth / captionimgwidth * captionimgheight) + 'px';
				jQuery(this).css({height: newcaptionheight}); 
				jQuery("div.wp-caption img").css({height: newcaptionimgheight}); 
				}
		});
		
		/* sfhover for LI:HOVER support in IE6: */
		jQuery("ul li").
			hover( function() {
					jQuery(this).addClass("sfhover")
				}, 
				function() {
					jQuery(this).removeClass("sfhover")
				} 
			); 

	/* End IE6 */
	}
	
	
	
	/* Since 3.7.8: Auto resize videos (embed and iframe elements) 
	TODO: Parse parent's dimensions only once per layout column, not per video
	*/
	function bfa_resize_video() {
		jQuery('embed, iframe').each( function() {
			var video = jQuery(this),
			videoWidth = video.attr('width'); // use the attr here, not width() or css()
			videoParent = video.parent(),
			videoParentWidth = parseFloat( videoParent.css( 'width' ) ),
			videoParentBorder = parseFloat( videoParent.css( 'border-left-width' ) ) 
										+  parseFloat( videoParent.css( 'border-right-width' ) ),
			videoParentPadding = parseFloat( videoParent.css( 'padding-left' ) ) 
										+  parseFloat( videoParent.css( 'padding-right' ) ),
			maxWidth = videoParentWidth - videoParentBorder - videoParentPadding;

			if( videoWidth > maxWidth ) {
				var videoHeight = video.attr('height'),
				videoMaxHeight = ( maxWidth / videoWidth * videoHeight );
				video.attr({ width: maxWidth, height: videoMaxHeight });
			} 

		});	
	}
	bfa_resize_video();
	jQuery(window).resize( bfa_resize_video );

		
	jQuery(".post table tr").
		mouseover(function() {
			jQuery(this).addClass("over");
		}).
		mouseout(function() {
			jQuery(this).removeClass("over");
		});

	
	jQuery(".post table tr:even").
		addClass("alt");

	
	jQuery("input.text, input.TextField, input.file, input.password, textarea").
		focus(function () {  
			jQuery(this).addClass("highlight"); 
		}).
		blur(function () { 
			jQuery(this).removeClass("highlight"); 
		})
	
	jQuery("input.inputblur").
		focus(function () {  
			jQuery(this).addClass("inputfocus"); 
		}).
		blur(function () { 
			jQuery(this).removeClass("inputfocus"); 
		})

		

	
	jQuery("input.button, input.Button, input#submit").
		mouseover(function() {
			jQuery(this).addClass("buttonhover");
		}).
		mouseout(function() {
			jQuery(this).removeClass("buttonhover");
		});

	/* toggle "you can use these xhtml tags" */
	jQuery("a.xhtmltags").
		click(function(){ 
			jQuery("div.xhtml-tags").slideToggle(300); 
		});

	/* For the Tabbed Widgets plugin: */
	jQuery("ul.tw-nav-list").
		addClass("clearfix");

		
	
});

//]]>

								<div class="post-22 post type-post status-publish format-standard hentry category-cpp-tutorial odd" id="post-22">
						<div class="post-headline">		<h1>1.3 &#8212; A first look at variables</h1>
		</div>		<div class="post-byline">By Alex, on May 30th, 2007</div>		<div class="post-bodycopy clearfix"><p><strong>Variables</strong></p>
<p>A statement such as <code>x = 5;</code> seems obvious enough.  As you would guess, we are assigning the value of 5 to x.  But what exactly is x?  x is a variable.</p>
<p>A <strong>variable</strong> in C++ is a name for a piece of memory that can be used to store information.  You can think of a variable as a mailbox, or a cubbyhole, where we can put and retrieve information.  All computers have memory, called RAM (random access memory), that is available for programs to use.  When a variable is defined, a piece of that memory is set aside for that variable.</p>
<p>In this section, we are only going to consider integer variables.  An <strong>integer</strong> is a whole number, such as 1, 2, 3, -1, -12, or 16.  An integer variable is a variable that holds an integer value.</p>
<p>In order to define a variable, we generally use a <strong>declaration statement</strong>.  Here&#8217;s an example of defining variable x as an integer variable (one that can hold integer values):</p><!-- Crayon Syntax Highlighter v2.7.1 -->

		<div id="crayon-555d73d4b3cfc610987203" class="crayon-syntax crayon-theme-familiar-learncppcom crayon-font-monaco crayon-os-pc print-yes notranslate" data-settings=" no-popup minimize scroll-mouseover wrap" style=" margin-top: 12px; margin-bottom: 12px; font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;">
		
			<div class="crayon-plain-wrap"></div>
			<div class="crayon-main" style="">
				<table class="crayon-table">
					<tr class="crayon-row">
				<td class="crayon-nums " data-settings="show">
					<div class="crayon-nums-content" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;"><div class="crayon-num" data-line="crayon-555d73d4b3cfc610987203-1">1</div></div>
				</td>
						<td class="crayon-code"><div class="crayon-pre" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important; -moz-tab-size:4; -o-tab-size:4; -webkit-tab-size:4; tab-size:4;"><div class="crayon-line" id="crayon-555d73d4b3cfc610987203-1"><span class="crayon-t">int</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-v">x</span><span class="crayon-sy">;</span></div></div></td>
					</tr>
				</table>
			</div>
		</div>
<!-- [Format Time: 0.0005 seconds] -->
<p></p>
<p>When this statement is executed by the CPU, a piece of memory from RAM will be set aside (called <strong>instantiation</strong>).  For the sake of example, let&#8217;s say that the variable x is assigned memory location 140.  Whenever the program sees the variable x in an expression or statement, it knows that it should look in memory location 140 to get the value.</p>
<p>One of the most common operations done with variables is assignment.  To do this, we use the assignment operator, more commonly known as the = symbol.  For example:</p>
<p></p><!-- Crayon Syntax Highlighter v2.7.1 -->

		<div id="crayon-555d73d4b3d0f588794867" class="crayon-syntax crayon-theme-familiar-learncppcom crayon-font-monaco crayon-os-pc print-yes notranslate" data-settings=" no-popup minimize scroll-mouseover wrap" style=" margin-top: 12px; margin-bottom: 12px; font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;">
		
			<div class="crayon-plain-wrap"></div>
			<div class="crayon-main" style="">
				<table class="crayon-table">
					<tr class="crayon-row">
				<td class="crayon-nums " data-settings="show">
					<div class="crayon-nums-content" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;"><div class="crayon-num" data-line="crayon-555d73d4b3d0f588794867-1">1</div></div>
				</td>
						<td class="crayon-code"><div class="crayon-pre" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important; -moz-tab-size:4; -o-tab-size:4; -webkit-tab-size:4; tab-size:4;"><div class="crayon-line" id="crayon-555d73d4b3d0f588794867-1"><span class="crayon-v">x</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-o">=</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-cn">5</span><span class="crayon-sy">;</span></div></div></td>
					</tr>
				</table>
			</div>
		</div>
<!-- [Format Time: 0.0005 seconds] -->
<p></p>
<p>When the CPU executes this statement, it translates this to &#8220;put the value of 5 in memory location 140&#8243;.</p>
<p>Later in our program, we could print that value to the screen using std::cout:</p>
<p></p><!-- Crayon Syntax Highlighter v2.7.1 -->

		<div id="crayon-555d73d4b3d16088140096" class="crayon-syntax crayon-theme-familiar-learncppcom crayon-font-monaco crayon-os-pc print-yes notranslate" data-settings=" no-popup minimize scroll-mouseover wrap" style=" margin-top: 12px; margin-bottom: 12px; font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;">
		
			<div class="crayon-plain-wrap"></div>
			<div class="crayon-main" style="">
				<table class="crayon-table">
					<tr class="crayon-row">
				<td class="crayon-nums " data-settings="show">
					<div class="crayon-nums-content" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;"><div class="crayon-num" data-line="crayon-555d73d4b3d16088140096-1">1</div></div>
				</td>
						<td class="crayon-code"><div class="crayon-pre" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important; -moz-tab-size:4; -o-tab-size:4; -webkit-tab-size:4; tab-size:4;"><div class="crayon-line" id="crayon-555d73d4b3d16088140096-1"><span class="crayon-v">std</span><span class="crayon-o">::</span><span class="crayon-r">cout</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-o">&lt;&lt;</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-v">x</span><span class="crayon-sy">;</span><span class="crayon-h">&nbsp;&nbsp;</span><span class="crayon-c">// prints the value of x (memory location 140) to the console</span></div></div></td>
					</tr>
				</table>
			</div>
		</div>
<!-- [Format Time: 0.0006 seconds] -->
<p></p>
<p><strong>l-values and r-values</strong></p>
<p>In C++, variables are a type of l-value (pronounced ell-values).  An <strong>l-value</strong> is a value that has an address (in memory).  Since all variables have addresses, all variables are l-values.  The name l-value came about because l-values are the only values that can be on the left side of an assignment statement.  When we do an assignment, the left hand side of the assignment operator must be an l-value.  Consequently, a statement like <code>5 = 6;</code> will cause a compile error, because 5 is not an l-value.  The value of 5 has no memory, and thus nothing can be assigned to it.  5 means 5, and its value can not be reassigned.  When an l-value has a value assigned to it, the current value as that memory address is overwritten.</p>
<p>The opposite of l-values are r-values (pronounced arr-values).  An <strong>r-value</strong> refers to any value that can be assigned to an l-value.  r-values are always evaluated to produce a single value.  Examples of r-values are single numbers (such as 5, which evaluates to 5), variables (such as x, which evaluates to whatever value was last assigned to it), or expressions (such as 2 + x, which evaluates to the value of x plus 2).</p>
<p>Here is an example of some assignment statements, showing how the r-values evaluate:</p><!-- Crayon Syntax Highlighter v2.7.1 -->

		<div id="crayon-555d73d4b3d1e346756293" class="crayon-syntax crayon-theme-familiar-learncppcom crayon-font-monaco crayon-os-pc print-yes notranslate" data-settings=" no-popup minimize scroll-mouseover wrap" style=" margin-top: 12px; margin-bottom: 12px; font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;">

				</td>

class="crayon-sy">;</span><span class="crayon-h">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;</span><span class="crayon-c">// 4 evaluates to 4, which is then assigned to y</span></div><div class="crayon-line" class="crayon-h">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;</span><span class="crayon-c">// define x as an integer variable</span></div><div class="crayon-line crayon-striped-line" (useless!)</span></div><div class="crayon-line crayon-striped-line" id="crayon-555d73d4b3d1e346756293-8"><span class="crayon-v">x</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-o">=</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-v">x</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-o">+</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span x.</span></div></div></td>
					</tr>
				</table>
			</div>
		</div>
<!-- [Format Time: 0.0048 seconds] -->
<p></p>
<p>Let&#8217;s take a closer look at the last assignment statement above, since it causes the most confusion.</p>
<p></p><!-- Crayon Syntax Highlighter v2.7.1 -->

		<div id="crayon-555d73d4b3d25508823136" class="crayon-syntax crayon-theme-familiar-learncppcom crayon-font-monaco crayon-os-pc print-yes notranslate" data-settings=" no-popup minimize scroll-mouseover wrap" style=" margin-top: 12px; margin-bottom: 12px; font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;">
		
			<div class="crayon-plain-wrap"></div>
			<div class="crayon-main" style="">
				<table class="crayon-table">
					<tr class="crayon-row">
				<td class="crayon-nums " data-settings="show">
					<div class="crayon-nums-content" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;"><div class="crayon-num" data-line="crayon-555d73d4b3d25508823136-1">1</div></div>
				</td>
						<td class="crayon-code"><div class="crayon-pre" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important; -moz-tab-size:4; -o-tab-size:4; -webkit-tab-size:4; tab-size:4;"><div class="crayon-line" id="crayon-555d73d4b3d25508823136-1"><span class="crayon-v">x</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-o">=</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-v">x</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-o">+</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-cn">1</span><span class="crayon-sy">;</span></div></div></td>
					</tr>
				</table>
			</div>
		</div>
<!-- [Format Time: 0.0006 seconds] -->
<p></p>
<p>In this statement, the variable x is being used in two different contexts.  On the left side of the assignment operator, &#8220;x&#8221; is being used as an l-value (variable with an address).  On the right side of the assignment operator, x is being used as an r-value, and will be evaluated to produce a value (in this case, 7).  When C++ evaluates the above statement, it evaluates as:</p>
<p></p><!-- Crayon Syntax Highlighter v2.7.1 -->

		<div id="crayon-555d73d4b3d2b192943070" class="crayon-syntax crayon-theme-familiar-learncppcom crayon-font-monaco crayon-os-pc print-yes notranslate" data-settings=" no-popup minimize scroll-mouseover wrap" style=" margin-top: 12px; margin-bottom: 12px; font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;">
		
			<div class="crayon-plain-wrap"></div>
			<div class="crayon-main" style="">
				<table class="crayon-table">
					<tr class="crayon-row">
				<td class="crayon-nums " data-settings="show">
					<div class="crayon-nums-content" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;"><div class="crayon-num" data-line="crayon-555d73d4b3d2b192943070-1">1</div></div>
				</td>
						<td class="crayon-code"><div class="crayon-pre" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important; -moz-tab-size:4; -o-tab-size:4; -webkit-tab-size:4; tab-size:4;"><div class="crayon-line" id="crayon-555d73d4b3d2b192943070-1"><span class="crayon-v">x</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-o">=</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-cn">7</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-o">+</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-cn">1</span><span class="crayon-sy">;</span></div></div></td>
					</tr>
				</table>
			</div>
		</div>
<!-- [Format Time: 0.0006 seconds] -->
<p></p>
<p>Which makes it obvious that C++ will assign the value 8 back into variable x.</p>
<p>Programmers don&#8217;t tend to talk about l-values or r-values much, so it&#8217;s not that important to remember the terms.  The key takeaway is that on the left side of the assignment, you must have something that represents a memory address (such as a variable).  Everything on the right side of the assignment will be evaluated to produce a value.</p>
<p><strong>Uninitialized variables</strong></p>
<p>Unlike some programming languages, C/C++ does not initialize variables to a given value (such as zero) automatically (for performance reasons).  Thus when a variable is assigned to a memory location by the compiler, the default value of that variable is whatever garbage happens to already be in that memory location!  A variable that has not been assigned a value is called an <strong>uninitialized variable</strong>.</p>
<p>Note: Some compilers, such as Visual Studio, <em>will</em> initialize the contents of memory when you&#8217;re using a debug build configuration.  This will not happen when using a release build configuration.</p>
<p>Uninitialized variables can lead to interesting (and by interesting, we mean unexpected) results.  Consider the following short program:</p>
<p></p><!-- Crayon Syntax Highlighter v2.7.1 -->

		<div id="crayon-555d73d4b3d32308102883" class="crayon-syntax crayon-theme-familiar-learncppcom crayon-font-monaco crayon-os-pc print-yes notranslate" data-settings=" no-popup minimize scroll-mouseover wrap" style=" margin-top: 12px; margin-bottom: 12px; font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;">
		
			<div class="crayon-plain-wrap"></div>
			<div class="crayon-main" style="">

				<td class="crayon-nums " data-settings="show">

				</td>
						<td class="crayon-code"><div class="crayon-pre" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important; -moz-tab-size:4; -o-tab-size:4; -webkit-tab-size:4; tab-size:4;"><div class="crayon-sy">)</span></div><div class="crayon-line" id="crayon-555d73d4b3d32308102883-5"><span class="crayon-sy">{</span></div><div class="crayon-line crayon-striped-line" id="crayon-555d73d4b3d32308102883-6"><span class="crayon-h">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;</span><span class="crayon-c">// define an integer variable named x</span></div><div class="crayon-line" id="crayon-555d73d4b3d32308102883-7"><span class="crayon-h">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;</span><span class="crayon-t">int</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-v">x</span><span class="crayon-sy">;</span></div><div class="crayon-line crayon-striped-line" id="crayon-555d73d4b3d32308102883-8"><span class="crayon-h">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;</span></div><div class="crayon-line" id="crayon-555d73d4b3d32308102883-9"><span class="crayon-h">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;</span><span class="crayon-c">// print the value of x to the screen (dangerous, because x is uninitialized)</span></div><div class="crayon-line crayon-striped-line" id="crayon-555d73d4b3d32308102883-10"><span class="crayon-h">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;</span><span class="crayon-v">std</span><span class="crayon-o">::</span><span class="crayon-r">cout</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-o">&lt;&lt;</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-v">x</span><span class="crayon-sy">;</span></div><div class="crayon-line" id="crayon-555d73d4b3d32308102883-11"><span class="crayon-sy">}</span></div></div></td>
					</tr>
				</table>
			</div>
		</div>
<!-- [Format Time: 0.0013 seconds] -->
<p></p>
<p>In this case, the computer will assign some unused memory to x.  It will then send the value residing in that memory location to cout, which will print the value.  But what value will it print?  The answer is &#8220;who knows!&#8221;, and the answer may change every time you run the program.  When the author ran this program with the Visual Studio 2013 compiler, std::cout printed the value <code>7177728</code> one time, and <code>5277592</code> the next.</p>
<p>A couple of notes if you want to run this program yourself:</p>
<ul>
<li>Make sure you&#8217;re using a release build configuration (see section <a href="http://www.learncpp.com/cpp-tutorial/06a-build-configurations/">0.6a -- Build configurations</a> for information on how to do that).  Otherwise the above program may print whatever value your compiler is initializing memory with (Visual Studio uses -858993460).</li>
<p></p>
<li>If your compiler won&#8217;t let you run this program because it flags variable x as an uninitialized variable, a possible solution to get around this issue is noted <a href="http://www.learncpp.com/cpp-tutorial/13-a-first-look-at-variables/#comment-251538">in the comments section</a>.</li>
</ul>
<p>Using uninitialized variables is one of the most common mistakes that novice programmers make, and unfortunately, it can also be one of the most challenging to debug (because the program may run fine anyway if the uninitialized value happened to get assigned to a spot of memory that had a reasonable value in it, like 0).</p>
<p>Fortunately, most modern compilers will print warnings at compile-time if they can detect a variable that is used without being initialized.  For example, compiling the above program on Visual Studio 2005 express produced the following warning:</p>
<p><code>c:vc2005projectstesttesttest.cpp(11) : warning C4700: uninitialized local variable 'x' used</code></p>
<p>A good rule of thumb is to assign values to variables when they are defined.  C++ makes this easy by letting you assign values on the same line as the declaration of the variable:</p><!-- Crayon Syntax Highlighter v2.7.1 -->

		<div id="crayon-555d73d4b3d3b031950567" class="crayon-syntax crayon-theme-familiar-learncppcom crayon-font-monaco crayon-os-pc print-yes notranslate" data-settings=" no-popup minimize scroll-mouseover wrap" style=" margin-top: 12px; margin-bottom: 12px; font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;">
		
			<div class="crayon-plain-wrap"></div>
			<div class="crayon-main" style="">
				<table class="crayon-table">
					<tr class="crayon-row">
				<td class="crayon-nums " data-settings="show">
					<div class="crayon-nums-content" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;"><div class="crayon-num" data-line="crayon-555d73d4b3d3b031950567-1">1</div></div>
				</td>
						<td class="crayon-code"><div class="crayon-pre" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important; -moz-tab-size:4; -o-tab-size:4; -webkit-tab-size:4; tab-size:4;"><div class="crayon-line" id="crayon-555d73d4b3d3b031950567-1"><span class="crayon-t">int</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-v">x</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-o">=</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-cn">0</span><span class="crayon-sy">;</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-c">// define integer variable x and assign the value of 0 to it.</span></div></div></td>
					</tr>
				</table>
			</div>
		</div>
<!-- [Format Time: 0.0004 seconds] -->
<p></p>
<p>This ensures that your variable will always have a consistent value, making it easier to debug if something goes wrong somewhere else.</p>
<p><em>Rule: Assign values to your variables when you define them.</em></p>
<p><strong>Quiz</strong><br />
What values does this program print?</p>

		July 10, 2009 at 7:15 pm</a>
        <span class="comment-reply-link"><a class='comment-reply-link' href='/cpp-tutorial/13-a-first-look-at-variables/?replytocom=64115#respond' onclick='return addComment.moveForm( "comment-64115", "64115", "respond", "22" )' aria-label='Reply to Quinn'> &middot; Reply</a></span>		 
		</div>
		<p>I disagree. This can very easily in larger programs cause cryptic errors from name conflicts. Keeping <b>using namespace</b> within functions limits it&#8217;s scope, and thus limits its potential for causing problems. The safest, though, is to simply always refer to the namespaces, i.e. &#8220;std::cout &lt;&lt;  x&#8221; instead.</p>
		</div>

		</div>
		<p>No, unfortunately it will not. His problem was that the program closed immediately after input. It is most likely because he has an IDE which breaks program execution immediately after main() returns 0. As such, he would need to either use a pause function such as system(&#8220;PAUSE&#8221;) to prompt the user to press enter, before the program breaks execution.</p>

					<div class="crayon-nums-content" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;"><div class="crayon-num" data-line="crayon-555d73d4b97ca390363440-1">1</div></div>
				</td>
						<td class="crayon-code"><div class="crayon-pre" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important; -moz-tab-size:4; -o-tab-size:4; -webkit-tab-size:4; tab-size:4;"><div class="crayon-line" id="crayon-555d73d4b97ca390363440-1"><span class="crayon-p">#include &lt;cstdlib&gt; &lt;!--formatted--&gt;</span></div></div></td>
					</tr>
				</table>
			</div>
		</div>
<!-- [Format Time: 0.0002 seconds] -->
<p></p>
<p>This will include the C standard library into your program.</p>
<p>Then, before the return statement in main(), add system(&#8220;PAUSE&#8221;), as such:</p>
<p></p><!-- Crayon Syntax Highlighter v2.7.1 -->

		<div id="crayon-555d73d4b97d5972534127" class="crayon-syntax crayon-theme-familiar-learncppcom crayon-font-monaco crayon-os-pc print-yes notranslate" data-settings=" no-popup minimize scroll-mouseover wrap" style=" margin-top: 12px; margin-bottom: 12px; font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;">
		
			<div class="crayon-plain-wrap"></div>
			<div class="crayon-main" style="">
				<table class="crayon-table">
					<tr class="crayon-row">
				<td class="crayon-nums " data-settings="show">
					<div class="crayon-nums-content" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;"><div class="crayon-num" data-line="crayon-555d73d4b97d5972534127-1">1</div><div class="crayon-num crayon-striped-num" data-line="crayon-555d73d4b97d5972534127-2">2</div><div class="crayon-num" data-line="crayon-555d73d4b97d5972534127-3">3</div><div class="crayon-num crayon-striped-num" data-line="crayon-555d73d4b97d5972534127-4">4</div><div class="crayon-num" data-line="crayon-555d73d4b97d5972534127-5">5</div><div class="crayon-num crayon-striped-num" data-line="crayon-555d73d4b97d5972534127-6">6</div><div class="crayon-num" data-line="crayon-555d73d4b97d5972534127-7">7</div><div class="crayon-num crayon-striped-num" data-line="crayon-555d73d4b97d5972534127-8">8</div></div>
				</td>
						<td class="crayon-code"><div class="crayon-pre" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important; -moz-tab-size:4; -o-tab-size:4; -webkit-tab-size:4; tab-size:4;"><div class="crayon-line" id="crayon-555d73d4b97d5972534127-1"><span class="crayon-t">int</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-e">main</span><span class="crayon-sy">(</span><span class="crayon-sy">)</span></div><div class="crayon-line crayon-striped-line" id="crayon-555d73d4b97d5972534127-2"><span class="crayon-sy">{</span></div><div class="crayon-line" id="crayon-555d73d4b97d5972534127-3"><span class="crayon-h">&nbsp;&nbsp; </span><span class="crayon-c">// Some code here...</span></div><div class="crayon-line crayon-striped-line" id="crayon-555d73d4b97d5972534127-4"><span class="crayon-h">&nbsp;&nbsp; </span></div><div class="crayon-line" id="crayon-555d73d4b97d5972534127-5"><span class="crayon-h">&nbsp;&nbsp; </span><span class="crayon-e">system</span><span class="crayon-sy">(</span><span class="crayon-s">"PAUSE"</span><span class="crayon-sy">)</span><span class="crayon-sy">;</span></div><div class="crayon-line crayon-striped-line" id="crayon-555d73d4b97d5972534127-6"><span class="crayon-h">&nbsp;&nbsp; </span><span class="crayon-st">return</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-cn">0</span><span class="crayon-sy">;</span></div><div class="crayon-line" id="crayon-555d73d4b97d5972534127-7"><span class="crayon-sy">}</span></div><div class="crayon-line crayon-striped-line" id="crayon-555d73d4b97d5972534127-8"><span class="crayon-o">&lt;</span><span class="crayon-o">!</span><span class="crayon-o">--</span><span class="crayon-v">formatted</span><span class="crayon-o">--</span><span class="crayon-o">&gt;</span></div></div></td>
					</tr>
				</table>
			</div>
		</div>
<!-- [Format Time: 0.0008 seconds] -->
<p></p>
<p>That should do it. However, the bad thing here is that I think this works ONLY on Windows&#8230;not good! Also, I have heard that the system() function is very unsafe and should generally be avoided in professional projects, which is perhaps not so important here because you are just studying.</p>
<p>Hope that helps! If you need more help you can mail me (csvanefalk@hushmail.me) or of course ask the owner of the site (Alex). Me and Alex are not affiliated in any way, I would just like to help out <img src="http://www.learncpp.com/blog/wp-includes/images/smilies/simple-smile.png" alt=":)" class="wp-smiley" style="height: 1em; max-height: 1em;" /> Dont forget to give the props to Alex for his great site though!</p>

		<p>first the line looks wrong<br />
it should be cout >> x;  not cout > x; </p>
<p>Second, the prg closes if you are using VS2005 or a similar IDE.  VS2005 creates a new console window when the program starts and closes it as soon as the program finishes.  The code executed perfectly.  Just that as soon as it prints the output, the program has finished and it closes leaving you no time to see it.  you need to make it pause using a &#8220;cin&#8221; function.</p>
<p>i wrote my own terminating code:</p>
<pre>//for terminating the application
	cout < <endl << endl << endl << "Type something and Press Enter to Terminate";
	string exitapp;
	cin >> exitapp;
	cout < < "terminating" <<endl;
	return 0; </PRE></pre>

<ul class="children">
		<li class="comment byuser comment-author-alex bypostauthor even depth-2 clearfix" id="comment-5555">
		<div id="div-comment-5555" class="clearfix comment-container bypostauthor">
		<div class="comment-author vcard">
		<img alt='' src='http://1.gravatar.com/avatar/a4e62d28c29f6c864923207d4c17993b?s=65&#038;d=mm&#038;r=g' srcset='http://1.gravatar.com/avatar/a4e62d28c29f6c864923207d4c17993b?s=130&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g 2x' class='avatar avatar-65 photo' height='65' width='65' />		<span class="authorname"><a href='http://www.tarindel.com' rel='external nofollow' class='url'>Alex</a></span>
		</div>
				<div class="comment-meta commentmetadata">
		<a href="http://www.learncpp.com/cpp-tutorial/13-a-first-look-at-variables/#comment-5555">
		January 5, 2008 at 10:10 am</a>
        <span class="comment-reply-link"><a class='comment-reply-link' href='/cpp-tutorial/13-a-first-look-at-variables/?replytocom=5555#respond' onclick='return addComment.moveForm( "comment-5555", "5555", "respond", "22" )' aria-label='Reply to Alex'> &middot; Reply</a></span>		 
		</div>
		<p>Memory is really just a sequence of binary bits strung together, and memory gets reused often.  So your int variable x might use the same memory location as some other variable was using just a moment ago.  If the variable x is not initialized, it &#8220;inherits&#8221; (in the non object-oriented sense) whatever value was there previously.</p>
<p>For example, let&#8217;s say there was 8 bits of memory that had this value: 0000 0101.</p>
<p>If you declared char chValue, and the variable chValue was assigned to this memory address, then chValue will start with the &#8220;uninitialized&#8221; value 5, because 0000 0101 binary = 5 decimal.</p>
<p>As a consequence of this, you never know what value an uninitialized variable will print because it depends on whatever happens to already be in memory the variable is using.  It may change every time you run the program.  It may change only occasionally.  But you can always count on it being something you don&#8217;t want!</p>
		</div>
</li><!-- #comment-## -->
</ul><!-- .children -->

		<li class="comment odd alt thread-odd thread-alt depth-1 clearfix" id="comment-5673">
		<div id="div-comment-5673" class="clearfix comment-container">

        <span class="comment-reply-link"><a class='comment-reply-link' href='/cpp-tutorial/13-a-first-look-at-variables/?replytocom=5673#respond' onclick='return addComment.moveForm( "comment-5673", "5673", "respond", "22" )' aria-label='Reply to renu'> &middot; Reply</a></span>		 
		</div>
		<p>My question is same as Chucks. I tried this and it is printing -858993460 . Why is it printing a particular number if it is a garbage value? Is there a specific reason for that? I tried it 3-4 times and every time it prints -858993460 .<br />
Thanks,<br />

<ul class="children">
		<li class="comment byuser comment-author-alex bypostauthor even depth-2 clearfix" id="comment-5675">
		<div id="div-comment-5675" class="clearfix comment-container bypostauthor">
		<div class="comment-author vcard">
		<img alt='' src='http://1.gravatar.com/avatar/a4e62d28c29f6c864923207d4c17993b?s=65&#038;d=mm&#038;r=g' srcset='http://1.gravatar.com/avatar/a4e62d28c29f6c864923207d4c17993b?s=130&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g 2x' class='avatar avatar-65 photo' height='65' width='65' />		<span class="authorname"><a href='http://www.tarindel.com' rel='external nofollow' class='url'>Alex</a></span>
		</div>
				<div class="comment-meta commentmetadata">
		<a href="http://www.learncpp.com/cpp-tutorial/13-a-first-look-at-variables/#comment-5675">
		January 7, 2008 at 2:04 pm</a>
        <span class="comment-reply-link"><a class='comment-reply-link' href='/cpp-tutorial/13-a-first-look-at-variables/?replytocom=5675#respond' onclick='return addComment.moveForm( "comment-5675", "5675", "respond", "22" )' aria-label='Reply to Alex'> &middot; Reply</a></span>		 
		</div>
		<p>Because this variable is not allocated dynamically, it&#8217;s being allocated on the stack.  Lots of stuff is put in the stack, including function call information, return addresses, etc&#8230; I presume (and this is just an educated guess) that the fact that we are all seeing the same number (-858993460) has something to do with the way the program or the OS is setting up the stack before the program begins executing.  Perhaps the OS is cleaning out the stack to ensure that we don&#8217;t &#8220;recover&#8221; sensitive information from a prior program&#8217;s execution?</p>
<p>As an aside, although -858993460 seems like a really bizarre number, it&#8217;s actually just 0xCCCCCCCC in hex (which is bit pattern 1100 1100 1100 1100 1100 1100 1100 1100).</p>
		</div>
</li><!-- #comment-## -->
		<li class="comment odd alt depth-2 clearfix" id="comment-39314">
		<div id="div-comment-39314" class="clearfix comment-container">
		<div class="comment-author vcard">
		<img alt='' src='http://2.gravatar.com/avatar/e514ad6a171fec9bf8dfad7ff71d9f9a?s=65&#038;d=mm&#038;r=g' srcset='http://2.gravatar.com/avatar/e514ad6a171fec9bf8dfad7ff71d9f9a?s=130&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g 2x' class='avatar avatar-65 photo' height='65' width='65' />		<span class="authorname">Tom</span>
		</div>
				<div class="comment-meta commentmetadata">
		<a href="http://www.learncpp.com/cpp-tutorial/13-a-first-look-at-variables/#comment-39314">
		January 26, 2009 at 1:40 pm</a>
        <span class="comment-reply-link"><a class='comment-reply-link' href='/cpp-tutorial/13-a-first-look-at-variables/?replytocom=39314#respond' onclick='return addComment.moveForm( "comment-39314", "39314", "respond", "22" )' aria-label='Reply to Tom'> &middot; Reply</a></span>		 
		</div>
		<p>This is feature of building debug C++ software with Visual Studio. Anything you don&#8217;t initialise yourself is set to 0xCCCCCCCC (interpreted as -858993460 if it&#8217;s an int).</p>
<p>Try switching the build type from debug to release, and the value will be truly uninitialised and may change each time you run it.</p>
		</div>
</li><!-- #comment-## -->

<p>int main ()<br />

    using namespace std;<br />
    int y;      // declare y as an integer variable<br />

    x = x + 1;  // x + 1 evaluates to 8, which is then assigned to x.<br />

		<div class="comment-author vcard">
		<img alt='' src='http://1.gravatar.com/avatar/a4e62d28c29f6c864923207d4c17993b?s=65&#038;d=mm&#038;r=g' srcset='http://1.gravatar.com/avatar/a4e62d28c29f6c864923207d4c17993b?s=130&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g 2x' class='avatar avatar-65 photo' height='65' width='65' />		<span class="authorname"><a href='http://www.tarindel.com' rel='external nofollow' class='url'>Alex</a></span>

		<a href="http://www.learncpp.com/cpp-tutorial/13-a-first-look-at-variables/#comment-7046">
		February 1, 2008 at 9:26 am</a>
        <span class="comment-reply-link"><a class='comment-reply-link' href='/cpp-tutorial/13-a-first-look-at-variables/?replytocom=7046#respond' onclick='return addComment.moveForm( "comment-7046", "7046", "respond", "22" )' aria-label='Reply to Alex'> &middot; Reply</a></span>		 
		</div>
		<p>Hi abdy.  This program shouldn&#8217;t output anything since you don&#8217;t have any cout statements, so I am not sure how you &#8220;keep getting 5 for the answer&#8221;.  If you are getting output, then I suspect you&#8217;re actually compiling and running a different project.  Some compilers let you keep multiple projects open simultaneously.  Make sure the project you want to compile is the active one (usually, right click on it and choose &#8220;set as active project&#8221; or something similar).</p>
<p>The cin.clear(); cin.ignore(255, &#8216;\n&#8217;); cin.get() lines just force the program to pause at the bottom so you can see the output before the window closes.</p>
		</div>

<p> </p>
<p>first of all, the whole &#8220;int caculate&#8221; part was compelely useless and unessary. second, &#8220;useing namespace std;&#8221; is suppost to be affter &#8220;int main ()&#8221;. third, many of your slash brackats  are wrong, when useing cout, all slash brackets are facing the left  . About the &#8220;system (&#8220;puase&#8221;)&#8221; part near the end, depending on what compiler you are useing you may not need it to be there. i&#8217;m useing a compiler that requires me to input a puase code. but even if your compiler dose not need it, it shoulden&#8217;t hurt anything.</p>

class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-e">pause</span><span class="crayon-sy">(</span><span class="crayon-sy">)</span></div><div class="crayon-line" id="crayon-555d73d4b997b092744233-9"><span class="crayon-sy">{</span></div><div class="crayon-line crayon-striped-line" id="crayon-555d73d4b997b092744233-10"><span class="crayon-h">	</span><span class="crayon-r">cout</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-o">&lt;&lt;</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-s">"Press any key to close this window..."</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-o">&lt;&lt;</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-v">endl</span><span class="crayon-sy">;</span></div><div class="crayon-line" id="crayon-555d73d4b997b092744233-11"><span class="crayon-h">	</span><span class="crayon-e">_getch</span><span class="crayon-sy">(</span><span class="crayon-sy">)</span><span class="crayon-sy">;</span></div><div class="crayon-line crayon-striped-line" id="crayon-555d73d4b997b092744233-12"><span class="crayon-sy">}</span></div><div class="crayon-line" </span><span class="crayon-e">main</span><span class="crayon-sy">(</span><span class="crayon-sy">)</span></div><div class="crayon-line" id="crayon-555d73d4b997b092744233-15"><span class="crayon-sy">{</span></div><div class="crayon-line crayon-striped-line" id="crayon-555d73d4b997b092744233-16"><span class="crayon-h">	</span><span class="crayon-r">cout</span><span class="crayon-o">&lt;&lt;</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-v">endl</span><span class="crayon-sy">;</span></div><div class="crayon-line" id="crayon-555d73d4b997b092744233-17"><span class="crayon-h">	</span></div><div class="crayon-line crayon-striped-line" id="crayon-555d73d4b997b092744233-18"><span class="crayon-h">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;</span><span class="crayon-e">pause</span><span class="crayon-sy">(</span><span class="crayon-sy">)</span><span class="crayon-sy">;</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-c">// Call our custom pause function before close</span></div><div class="crayon-line" class="crayon-sy">}</span></div></div></td>
					</tr>
				</table>
			</div>
		</div>
<!-- [Format Time: 0.0018 seconds] -->
<p></p>
<p>They said their reasoning is it would be cross platform compilable, because pause.exe is windows specific, and also if someone / something were to tamper with pause.exe, executing pause.exe could be dangerous.</p>
<p>It seems to work well, what are your thoughts / opinions on it?</p>
		</div>
<ul class="children">
		<li class="comment byuser comment-author-alex bypostauthor odd alt depth-2 clearfix" id="comment-59765">
		<div id="div-comment-59765" class="clearfix comment-container bypostauthor">
		<div class="comment-author vcard">
		<img alt='' src='http://1.gravatar.com/avatar/a4e62d28c29f6c864923207d4c17993b?s=65&#038;d=mm&#038;r=g' srcset='http://1.gravatar.com/avatar/a4e62d28c29f6c864923207d4c17993b?s=130&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g 2x' class='avatar avatar-65 photo' height='65' width='65' />		<span class="authorname"><a href='http://www.tarindel.com' rel='external nofollow' class='url'>Alex</a></span>

		May 1, 2009 at 9:36 pm</a>
        <span class="comment-reply-link"><a class='comment-reply-link' href='/cpp-tutorial/13-a-first-look-at-variables/?replytocom=59765#respond' onclick='return addComment.moveForm( "comment-59765", "59765", "respond", "22" )' aria-label='Reply to Alex'> &middot; Reply</a></span>		 
		</div>
		<p>It&#8217;ll work in the majority of cases, and yes, it&#8217;s better than using pause.exe.</p>
<p>The only time it&#8217;ll fail is if there are extra characters in the input buffer -- _getch() will read them and not stop for more input.</p>
<p>I present a slightly improved version of this in <a href="http://www.learncpp.com/cpp-tutorial/07-a-few-common-cpp-problems/" rel="nofollow">lesson 0.7 -- a few common cpp problems</a> that fixes that particular issue.</p>
<p>Sadly enough, the pausing issue is by far the most common topic on this site. <img src="http://www.learncpp.com/blog/wp-includes/images/smilies/simple-smile.png" alt=":)" class="wp-smiley" style="height: 1em; max-height: 1em;" /></p>
		</div>

<p>I keep getting an error message: error C4430: missing type specifier - int assumed. Note: C++ does not support default-int<br />
and error C2065: &#8216;cout&#8217; : undeclared identifier<br />
and error C2065: &#8216;endl&#8217; : undeclared identifier<br />
I don&#8217;t know why the first one getting numbers worked fine but this one does not at all, all i tried to do was erase the old stuff and enter the new stuff.</p>

class="crayon-st">return</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-cn">0</span><span class="crayon-sy">;</span></div><div class="crayon-line" id="crayon-555d73d4b9066243231283-21">&nbsp;</div><div class="crayon-line crayon-striped-line" id="crayon-555d73d4b9066243231283-22"><span class="crayon-sy">}</span></div></div></td>
					</tr>
				</table>
			</div>
		</div>
<!-- [Format Time: 0.0025 seconds] -->
<p></p>
<p>It doesn&#8217;t seem to like words. Whenever you type your name in it gives you a bunch of numbers back&#8230; is there anything I can do?</p>
		</div>

When I build essentially the same code in the IDE it builds fine and runs but when I put in a number and hit enter it just goes to a new line. It doesn&#8217;t display anything back to the screen and keeps running, I have to kill it manually.<br />

</span><span class="crayon-cn">0</span><span class="crayon-sy">;</span></div><div class="crayon-line" id="crayon-555d73d4b8f2d252333808-13"><span class="crayon-sy">}</span></div><div class="crayon-line crayon-striped-line" id="crayon-555d73d4b8f2d252333808-14"><span class="crayon-o">&lt;</span><span class="crayon-o">!</span><span class="crayon-o">--</span><span class="crayon-v">formatted</span><span class="crayon-o">--</span><span class="crayon-o">&gt;</span></div></div></td>
					</tr>
				</table>
			</div>
		</div>

<p></p>
<p>I&#8217;m going to dig into the IDE help next, and see if I can figure it out. I&#8217;m an engineering student and have been programming extensively in Fortran, so an editor and terminal is just fine by me, but I think an IDE is going to be essential if I want to make a jump to GUI applications.<br />
The professors say &#8220;if you can program in Fortran you can program in anything&#8221;, and it seems like C++ is the backbone of just about everything. Most people don&#8217;t care about things like Romberg integration or finite difference in a 3d matrix they just want a pretty window on their computer screen that gives them an answer. So, I&#8217;m off to learn C++ and this is the best tutorial I&#8217;ve found, thanx Alex.<br />
Anybody have suggestions on how to make this IDE behave?</p>

int doubleNumber(int x)

int _tmain(int argc, _TCHAR* argv[])
{
	using namespace std;	
	int x;
	cin &gt;&gt; x;
	cout &lt;&lt; doubleNumber(x)&lt;&lt;endl;
	x = doubleNumber(x);
	cout &lt;&lt; x&lt;&lt;endl;

		<div id="div-comment-97122" class="clearfix comment-container">
		<div class="comment-author vcard">
		<img alt='' src='http://0.gravatar.com/avatar/364c505e5c76db3f58368fa4ebf77a5c?s=65&#038;d=mm&#038;r=g' srcset='http://0.gravatar.com/avatar/364c505e5c76db3f58368fa4ebf77a5c?s=130&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g 2x' class='avatar avatar-65 photo' height='65' width='65' />		<span class="authorname">senthil</span>
		</div>
				<div class="comment-meta commentmetadata">
		<a href="http://www.learncpp.com/cpp-tutorial/13-a-first-look-at-variables/#comment-97122">
		March 21, 2012 at 3:52 am</a>
        <span class="comment-reply-link"><a class='comment-reply-link' href='/cpp-tutorial/13-a-first-look-at-variables/?replytocom=97122#respond' onclick='return addComment.moveForm( "comment-97122", "97122", "respond", "22" )' aria-label='Reply to senthil'> &middot; Reply</a></span>		 
		</div>
		<p>you are printing the local copy of &#8216;a&#8217; and not the return value. The local copy of &#8216;a&#8217; is initialized to 0 and not changed anywhere in the main. hence 0 is displayed.</p>
<p>solution:<br />
update the local copy of &#8216;a&#8217; with the return value.</p>
<p><code><br />
	a = input1(a);<br />
	cout &lt;&lt; a;<br />
</code></p>
		</div>

		</div>
		<p>Or simply pass the variable to input1() by reference instead of by value. Like this:</p>
<p><code><br />
#include &lt;iostream&gt;</p>
<p>void input1(int&amp; a)<br />
{<br />
	using namespace std;<br />
	cin &gt;&gt; a;<br />
}<br />
int main()<br />
{<br />
	using namespace std;<br />
	int a = 0;<br />
	input1(a);<br />
	cout &lt;&lt; a;</p>
<p>	return 0;<br />
}</code></p>

#include &lt;iostream&gt;</p>
<p>int main()<br />
{<br />
    using namespace std;<br />
    int x = 5;<br />
	x = x - 2;<br />
	cout &lt;&lt; x &lt;&lt; endl; //#1<br />
    cin.clear ();<br />
	cin.ignore(255, &#039;\n&#039;);<br />
	cin.get ();<br />
	int y = x;<br />
	cout &lt;&lt; y &lt;&lt; endl; //#2<br />
    cin.clear ();<br />
	cin.ignore(255, &#039;\n&#039;);<br />
	cin.get ();<br />
	cout &lt;&lt; x + y &lt;&lt; endl; //#3<br />
	cin.clear ();<br />
	cin.ignore(255, &#039;\n&#039;);<br />
	cin.get ();<br />
	cout &lt;&lt; x &lt;&lt; endl; //#4<br />
	cin.clear ();<br />
	cin.ignore(255, &#039;\n&#039;);<br />
	cin.get ();<br />
	int z;<br />
	cout &lt;&lt; z &lt;&lt; endl; //#5<br />
	cin.clear ();<br />
	cin.ignore(255, &#039;\n&#039;);<br />
	cin.get ();<br />
	return 0;</p>
<p>}<br />

    using namespace std;<br />
	cout&lt;&gt;x;<br />
	cout&lt;&lt; &quot;You Entered&quot;&lt;&lt; x &lt;&lt;endl;<br />
	return 0;<br />
}</p>
		</div>

int main()<br />
{<br />
using namespace std;</p>

e = b*10;</p>

l = e/100;</p>

a = e+b;</p>

m = b+l;</p>
<p>cout &lt;&lt; b &lt;&lt; e &lt;&lt; l &lt;&lt; a &lt;&lt; d &lt;&lt; s &lt;&lt; m;</p>

<ul class="children">
		<li class="comment byuser comment-author-alex bypostauthor even depth-2 clearfix" id="comment-251080">
		<div id="div-comment-251080" class="clearfix comment-container bypostauthor">
		<div class="comment-author vcard">
		<img alt='' src='http://1.gravatar.com/avatar/a4e62d28c29f6c864923207d4c17993b?s=65&#038;d=mm&#038;r=g' srcset='http://1.gravatar.com/avatar/a4e62d28c29f6c864923207d4c17993b?s=130&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g 2x' class='avatar avatar-65 photo' height='65' width='65' />		<span class="authorname">Alex</span>
		</div>
				<div class="comment-meta commentmetadata">
		<a href="http://www.learncpp.com/cpp-tutorial/13-a-first-look-at-variables/#comment-251080">
		January 4, 2015 at 12:15 pm</a>
        <span class="comment-reply-link"><a class='comment-reply-link' href='/cpp-tutorial/13-a-first-look-at-variables/?replytocom=251080#respond' onclick='return addComment.moveForm( "comment-251080", "251080", "respond", "22" )' aria-label='Reply to Alex'> &middot; Reply</a></span>		 
		</div>
		<p>main() is preceded by int because it returns an integer value to the operating system when the program terminates.</p>
<p>I talk about this in section <a href="http://www.learncpp.com/cpp-tutorial/14-a-first-look-at-functions/" rel="nofollow">1.4 -- a first look at functions</a>.</p>
<p>void main() is invalid C++ (although some Microsoft compilers accept it).  Your reference books are incorrect.</p>
		</div>

		<p>&#8220;One common trick that experienced programmers use is to assign the variable an initial value that is outside the range of meaningful values for that variable. For example, if we had a variable to store the number of cats the old lady down the street has, we might do the following:</p>
<p>1<br />
int cats = -1;<br />
Having -1 cats makes no sense. So if later, we did this:</p>
<p>1<br />
cout &lt;&lt; cats &lt;&lt; &quot; cats&quot; &lt;&lt; endl;<br />
and it printed -1 cats, we know that the variable was never assigned a real value correctly.&quot;</p>

		<p>Imaging you&#8217;re writing a program where you&#8217;re keeping track of how many cats are being adopted out today.</p>
<p></p><!-- Crayon Syntax Highlighter v2.7.1 -->

		<div id="crayon-555d73d4b7f63336560303" class="crayon-syntax crayon-theme-familiar-learncppcom crayon-font-monaco crayon-os-pc print-yes notranslate" data-settings=" no-popup minimize scroll-mouseover wrap" style=" margin-top: 12px; margin-bottom: 12px; font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;">

<p></p>
<p>You run the program, and it prints, &#8220;We adopted out 0 cats today!&#8221;.  Is this correct, or have you made an error somewhere and done a calculation wrong?  It&#8217;s not clear.</p>
<p>Now consider this program:</p>
<p></p><!-- Crayon Syntax Highlighter v2.7.1 -->

		<div id="crayon-555d73d4b7f6e649010509" class="crayon-syntax crayon-theme-familiar-learncppcom crayon-font-monaco crayon-os-pc print-yes notranslate" data-settings=" no-popup minimize scroll-mouseover wrap" style=" margin-top: 12px; margin-bottom: 12px; font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;">
		
			<div class="crayon-plain-wrap"></div>
			<div class="crayon-main" style="">
				<table class="crayon-table">
					<tr class="crayon-row">
				<td class="crayon-nums " data-settings="show">
					<div class="crayon-nums-content" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;"><div class="crayon-num" data-line="crayon-555d73d4b7f6e649010509-1">1</div><div class="crayon-num crayon-striped-num" data-line="crayon-555d73d4b7f6e649010509-2">2</div><div class="crayon-num" data-line="crayon-555d73d4b7f6e649010509-3">3</div><div class="crayon-num crayon-striped-num" data-line="crayon-555d73d4b7f6e649010509-4">4</div><div class="crayon-num" data-line="crayon-555d73d4b7f6e649010509-5">5</div></div>
				</td>
						<td class="crayon-code"><div class="crayon-pre" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important; -moz-tab-size:4; -o-tab-size:4; -webkit-tab-size:4; tab-size:4;"><div class="crayon-line" id="crayon-555d73d4b7f6e649010509-1"><span class="crayon-v">nCats</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-o">=</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-o">-</span><span class="crayon-cn">1</span><span class="crayon-sy">;</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-c">// We can't adopt out a negative number of cats</span></div><div class="crayon-line crayon-striped-line" id="crayon-555d73d4b7f6e649010509-2">&nbsp;</div><div class="crayon-line" id="crayon-555d73d4b7f6e649010509-3"><span class="crayon-c">// Do some stuff here</span></div><div class="crayon-line crayon-striped-line" id="crayon-555d73d4b7f6e649010509-4">&nbsp;</div><div class="crayon-line" id="crayon-555d73d4b7f6e649010509-5"><span class="crayon-r">cout</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-o">&lt;&lt;</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-s">"We adopted out &lt;&lt; nCats &lt;&lt; "</span><span class="crayon-e">cats </span><span class="crayon-v">today</span><span class="crayon-o">!</span>"<span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-o">&lt;&lt;</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-v">endl</span><span class="crayon-sy">;</span></div></div></td>
					</tr>
				</table>
			</div>
		</div>
<!-- [Format Time: 0.0008 seconds] -->
<p></p>
<p>If the code prints, &#8220;We adopted out 0 cats today!&#8221;, you know you really didn&#8217;t adopt out any cats.<br />
If the code prints, &#8220;We adopted out -1 cats today!&#8221;, you know there&#8217;s a problem in your program somewhere, because nCats should have never been left with the value of -1.</p>

		<p>Initialising a (real) variable with -1 is in my opinion not the best practice.<br />
For performance one may choose a unsigned datatype and -1 will not work with this? So you will have to switch to signed just to be able to tell if it&#8217;s declared?</p>
<p>Any better options? Probably declaring with a standard value or 0?</p>

        <span class="comment-reply-link"><a class='comment-reply-link' href='/cpp-tutorial/13-a-first-look-at-variables/?replytocom=251531#respond' onclick='return addComment.moveForm( "comment-251531", "251531", "respond", "22" )' aria-label='Reply to Catreece'> &middot; Reply</a></span>		 
		</div>
		<p>Disappointment get.</p>
<p>Saw the program to spit out whatever number X gets defined to and decided to run it myself out of curiousity. It would seem Visual Studio 2013 has since fixed this issue and will refuse to compile, stating that X is undefined.</p>
<p>Shame, that. It would&apos;ve been the first thing I did every time I sat down to learn more programming stuff, just test to see what X is today.</p>
<p>I wonder if there&apos;s any way to get around the error?</p>
<p>error C4700: uninitialized local variable &apos;x&apos; used</p>
<p>It used to work on older versions, so this implies that something about the source code of the compiler changed to look for that issue, which&apos;s a good thing, mostly. It also implies that it may therefore be possible to flat out tell it to run that line and ignore whatever errors it gets.</p>
<p>&#8230;Actually, now I&apos;m also curious if it&apos;s GOOD or BAD that I&apos;m actively trying to think of ways to break the compiler for my own entertainment&#8230; Probably bad. Oh well.</p>
		</div>

		<p>-858993460 is the value that Visual Studio initializes memory with when running programs in a debug configuration.</p>
<p>Switch to the release configuration (See section <a href="http://www.learncpp.com/cpp-tutorial/06a-build-configurations/" rel="nofollow">0.6a -- Build configurations</a> if you need help on how to do that) and try again.</p>

<p></p>

		<p>Is it acceptable to take advantage of the ability to use an uninitialized value and use it for a pseudorandom function?</p>
		</div>
<ul class="children">
		<li class="comment byuser comment-author-alex bypostauthor odd alt depth-2 clearfix" id="comment-252106">
		<div id="div-comment-252106" class="clearfix comment-container bypostauthor">
		<div class="comment-author vcard">
		<img alt='' src='http://1.gravatar.com/avatar/a4e62d28c29f6c864923207d4c17993b?s=65&#038;d=mm&#038;r=g' srcset='http://1.gravatar.com/avatar/a4e62d28c29f6c864923207d4c17993b?s=130&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g 2x' class='avatar avatar-65 photo' height='65' width='65' />		<span class="authorname">Alex</span>
		</div>
				<div class="comment-meta commentmetadata">
		<a href="http://www.learncpp.com/cpp-tutorial/13-a-first-look-at-variables/#comment-252106">
		April 9, 2015 at 11:48 am</a>
        <span class="comment-reply-link"><a class='comment-reply-link' href='/cpp-tutorial/13-a-first-look-at-variables/?replytocom=252106#respond' onclick='return addComment.moveForm( "comment-252106", "252106", "respond", "22" )' aria-label='Reply to Alex'> &middot; Reply</a></span>		 
		</div>
		<p>This isn&#8217;t a good idea.  The behavior of uninitialized variables is undefined, so you can&#8217;t assume anything about them, including whether they&#8217;ll be suitably unpredictable!</p>
<p>If you want a pseudorandom generator, use a well established one, like Mersenne Twister.  See section <a href="http://www.learncpp.com/cpp-tutorial/59-random-number-generation/" rel="nofollow"> 5.9 -- Random number generation</a> for more information about this.</p>
		</div>

And what I thought was it would be a wrong code because x assigned to 5 which means the last defined variable equals to 5=5-3 which means can&#8217;t be true.And when I checked the answer, it&#8217;s output was 3.An another question is the code written in the quiz section wouldn&#8217;t have  a { at the beginning of the code (I mean after main() function) and } at the end of the code ? .I would be very happy with your answer AND THANK YOU.</p>

		<p>Good question.  In the statement:</p><!-- Crayon Syntax Highlighter v2.7.1 -->

		<div id="crayon-555d73d4b7798122815751" class="crayon-syntax crayon-theme-familiar-learncppcom crayon-font-monaco crayon-os-pc print-yes notranslate" data-settings=" no-popup minimize scroll-mouseover wrap" style=" margin-top: 12px; margin-bottom: 12px; font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;">
		
			<div class="crayon-plain-wrap"></div>
			<div class="crayon-main" style="">
				<table class="crayon-table">
					<tr class="crayon-row">
				<td class="crayon-nums " data-settings="show">
					<div class="crayon-nums-content" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;"><div class="crayon-num" data-line="crayon-555d73d4b7798122815751-1">1</div></div>
				</td>
						<td class="crayon-code"><div class="crayon-pre" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important; -moz-tab-size:4; -o-tab-size:4; -webkit-tab-size:4; tab-size:4;"><div class="crayon-line" id="crayon-555d73d4b7798122815751-1"><span class="crayon-v">x</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-o">=</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-v">x</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-o">-</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-cn">2</span><span class="crayon-sy">;</span></div></div></td>
					</tr>
				</table>
			</div>
		</div>
<!-- [Format Time: 0.0005 seconds] -->
<p></p>
<p>x is being used in two different contexts.  On the left side, x is being used as an l-value (variable).  On the right side, x is being used as an r-value, and is being evaluated only for its value.</p>
<p>So C++ isn&#8217;t evaluating this as &#8220;5 = 5 - 2&#8243;, it&#8217;s evaluating it as &#8220;x = 5 - 2&#8243;, which makes a lot more sense.  I&#8217;ll try to clarify this in the lesson itself.</p>
		</div>
</li><!-- #comment-## -->
</ul><!-- .children -->
</li><!-- #comment-## -->
